  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ea1f863e-9e0e-4164-9641-53cf278935ec'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7326195008182944420" style="display:none"><b>In this unforgettable seventh book, Sophie must let the past and present blur together, because the deadliest secrets are always the ones that get erased.</b><br /><br />Sophie Foster doesn’t know what—or whom—to believe. And in a game with this many players, the worst mistake can be focusing on the wrong threat.<br /><br />But when the Neverseen prove that Sophie’s far more vulnerable than she ever imagined, she realizes it’s time to change the rules. Her powerful abilities can only protect her so far. To face down ruthless enemies, she must learn to fight.<br /><br />Unfortunately, battle training can’t help a beloved friend who’s facing a whole different danger—where the only solution involves one of the biggest risks Sophie and her friends have ever taken. And the distraction might be exactly what the villains have been waiting for.</span>

Yay!<br /><br />Q<br />“Ugh, you guys have really out-sparkled yourselves with this place. (c)<br />Q<br />“Do you think it’s weird to punish someone for crimes they don’t remember committing?” … Alvar’s future is being decided by a past he doesn’t believe is his.”(c)<br />Q<br />for the first time, she understood why people often paired the word “handsome” with “devastating.” His white-blond hair grew to a dramatic widow’s peak, adding a severity to his perfectly chiseled features. But it was his eyes that demanded the most attention. Dark as a midnight sky and shining with an intensity that could only come from millennia of wisdom.(c)<br />Q<br />I prefer the solace of home. It’s the only place where my mind doesn’t struggle to separate what is from what used to be. (c)<br />Q<br />...things from our past are often more than they seem.(c)<br />Q<br />“The lake was so serene at night, the way it reflected the stars. It was the perfect place to let my mind rest after a long day of bending the sun.”(c)<br />Q<br />“It’s quite tragic to think how often crucial choices come down to our best guess.”(c)<br />Q<br />“Generally, the most powerful plans are also the simplest.”(c)<br />Q<br />He was so determined to be angry that it was honestly kind of adorable. (c)<br />Q<br />She’d spent weeks stressing about how little they were accomplishing, and Dex had used that same time to build secret weapon stashes? (c)<br />Q<br />“How many weeks do you think the new guard would last before they’d run screaming back to Gildingham?” (c)<br />Q<br />“Everybody out! Lord Funkyhair needs a pep talk.” (c)<br />Q<br />“Um, are you living a double life as a creepy Shade? Because that’s who messed me up.” (c)<br />Q<br />“You’re saying this is a sixth element?” Magnate Leto clarified. “Earth, wind, water, fire, quintessence, and . . . shadowflux?” …<br />Just as fire hungers and wind breathes and water roars and earth waits. I’ve never been near quintessence, but I hear it pulses. And shadowflux dreams—hovering high above, waiting for something to capture its interest. (c)<br />Q<br />Everyone would rather sweep the knowledge away, bury it with the other bits and pieces that don’t fit within the neat box we use to define our world. But that won’t stop it from existing. Just like it won’t stop a few brave souls from reaching for the sky, calling for that pure, raw darkness. (c)<br />Q<br />Safe nor deadly. It is all things, waiting to discover how it will be wielded. What you do with it is entirely up to you. (c)<br />Q<br />But darkness is vital—and not because it teaches us to appreciate the light. It’s part of everything we know, and we’ve only begun to harness its potential. (c)<br />Q<br />A sliver of shade on a scorching day.<br />The first wisps of a long, quiet night.<br />The shadow of a perfect hiding space. (c)<br />Q<br />There’s greatness in you, Tam. But it will never amount to anything unless you embrace it. (c)<br />Q<br />Do you realize you look like a cornered gremlin whenever you have to talk about this?<br />Gee, thanks.<br />What? Gremlins are cute. (c)<br />Q<br />The motherly alicorn insisted on sorting through Sophie’s recent memories, catching every single one of the doubts and worries that Sophie was trying to bury. And instead of the usual flying dreams, she filled Sophie’s head with images of them galloping through the white-capped rapids of a surging river—cold water crashing into them. The currents tried to drag them under, but they kept their legs moving, kept their heads above the surface because they were stronger and faster and more powerful than anything the river could throw at them. (c)<br />Q<br />I guess the imaginary pieces of memory are all in the imaginary box now … (с)<br />Q<br />And wait a minute—I just realized we’re Legacy Buddies! It’ll be way more entertaining if he’s all loopy.” (с)<br />Q<br />But if you forget to reach out, I swear Fitz and I will find a way to smack you with our brains. <div id="review_2530460613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2530460613" />
    <a title="Maddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60336580-maddie"><img alt="Maddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498658110p2/60336580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2530460613?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/60336580-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2530460613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer877974515399382038">1.5/2<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478569549ra/21085284.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/><br/>- This book is over EIGHT HUNDRED PAGES. <br/><br/>- Half of it takes place while the narrator is bedridden. <br/><br/>- We do not get answers to even a quarter of the questions raised in this book, and we only get answers to ONE of the twenty plus lingering questions from previous books. <br/><br/>- Keefe was shortchanged. As were Biana, Dex, and Linh. And Wylie. And all of the adult characters other than Elwin. <br/><br/>- I have never seen romance derail a fantasy book's plot this badly. And I've read a lot of f</span></span>
  <span id="freeText877974515399382038" style="display:none">1.5/2<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478569549ra/21085284.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>- This book is over EIGHT HUNDRED PAGES. <br><br>- Half of it takes place while the narrator is bedridden. <br><br>- We do not get answers to even a quarter of the questions raised in this book, and we only get answers to ONE of the twenty plus lingering questions from previous books. <br><br>- Keefe was shortchanged. As were Biana, Dex, and Linh. And Wylie. And all of the adult characters other than Elwin. <br><br>- I have never seen romance derail a fantasy book's plot this badly. And I've read a lot of fantasy. <br><br>- I <i>KNEW</i> the Neverseen were going to try to recruit Tam. I get why, but it's just unneeded. We've already had someone join the Neverseen, we don't need to go down that road again. There are also so many dangling plot threads and only two books left. <br><br>- Fitz has always been a character I have struggled to like (or even just to care about). I think a big part of that is because he really isn’t likeable in the first two books (especially in Book 2), and because I’ve always felt that he has ulterior motives for pretty much everything he does (including his miraculous change of heart in Book 3). I was really hoping this book would endear him to me, but it didn’t. It’s hard for me to feel sorry for him re: Alvar given the terrible family situations the majority of the main cast has to deal with (this is even pointed out within the text). The fact that he’s the oldest main character (I’m pretty certain he’s 17 in this book) makes it even harder for me to swallow his behaviour. I say this as someone who absolutely understands how difficult is to have siblings you don’t like and feel are getting a free pass from your parents. Him making snippy comments to Keefe throughout the book (like that one about Keefe’s mom? Yeah, you don’t say that to a friend, let alone your alleged best friend) and calling Dex’s invention junk didn’t help matters.<br><br>- Relatedly, I’ve always felt Fitz's dynamic with Sophie relied a lot more on telling than showing, given that she’s always had a crush on him. Nothing that happened between them felt exciting or compelling because I haven't really been <i>shown</i> their relationship develop, I've been <i>told</i> everything about their relationship. I shouldn't be checking my watch when people are confessing their feelings. <br><br>- Gethen trying to cajole Fitz into killing Alvar is easily the most compelling scene in the book. If Fitz had done it, it might have made him an interesting character. <br><br>- Fitz admitting to leaving Alvar to drown, however, wasn’t nearly as interesting. It happens off screen, and felt like a bit of a cop-out. And of course, Alvar isn’t actually dead. OF COURSE. And I'm sure that Fitz is going to free pass for that in the next book (because being a cute boy gets you a free pass for everything from verbal abuse to attempted murder in this series!). God forbid we actually get a nuanced discussion about morality and difficult choices!<br><br>- <i>That’s</i> the Vacker legacy? Really? <i>Really?</i> I’m pretty sure the Vacker legacy is low blows and "taking the easy way out", as Keefe so aptly put it. <br><br>- Umber’s entire character/death reminds me of how George Lucas set Count Dooku up as this ‘epic’ villain, before unceremoniously killing him off five minutes into <i>Revenge of the Sith</i>. <br><br>- I have a theory about what's going on between Fitz and Keefe (and Alden...) and if I'm right...oh boy...<br><br>Overall: This should have been the first stepping stone to the finale, but it read like a book in the middle of a series. The plot was almost non-existent and the vast majority of the book felt like filler. The romance was a huge drag and the majority of the main cast was sidelined. Whereas the other books I have disliked (Book 1, Book 4, and Book 6) all had strong moments to balance out the bad (especially Book 4), this book didn't. <br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="877974515399382038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2420459415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420459415" />
    <a title="Ethence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20811978-ethence"><img alt="Ethence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541317072p2/20811978.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2420459415?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420459415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7529876662096783171">I am aware that this definitely won't be a popular opinion and that a lot of people are gonna disagree with me but...<br/><br/>PLEASE GIVE DEX AND BIANA MORE LOVE.<br/><br/>I loved the book and have been in the fandom since Exile came out and I gotta say, I really loved the Keefe Sencen back in KOTLC and Exile better. From Neverseen, we can clearly see how much development Shannon has given Keefe. And I get that he has been flirting with Sophie since KOTLC and I honestly don't mind it but too much of anything is ne</span>
  <span id="freeText7529876662096783171" style="display:none">I am aware that this definitely won't be a popular opinion and that a lot of people are gonna disagree with me but...<br /><br />PLEASE GIVE DEX AND BIANA MORE LOVE.<br /><br />I loved the book and have been in the fandom since Exile came out and I gotta say, I really loved the Keefe Sencen back in KOTLC and Exile better. From Neverseen, we can clearly see how much development Shannon has given Keefe. And I get that he has been flirting with Sophie since KOTLC and I honestly don't mind it but too much of anything is never good. Maybe it's just me but I feel that there's just too much of Keefe lately and not enough Fitz, Dex, Biana lately. <br /><br />PLEASE GIVE US SOME GURL LOVE. <br /><br />Sophie technically only is close to Fitz and Keefe and ever since the infamous kiss (actually since Neverseen), Dex has been rarely mentioned unless they needed help with his abilities. <br /><br />I can't say much about the plot but for relationships wise, IF THE ROMANCE WAS TONED DOWN SIGNIFICANTLY AND SOPHIES PERSONAL RELATIONSHIPS WITH BIANA AND DEX ARE IMPROVED I WOULD EXPLODE WITH GIDDINESS. <br /><br />Also, Fitz. Keefe had his fair share (okay, not really fair) of development but IT'S TIME FITZ HAD SOME TOO. (Besides the time in exile where we literally only learnt that Fitz's default was 'angry' and that he gives gifts and are cognates with Sophie) <br /><br />Okay, now for the twins. I absolutely adore Tam and how he overprotects Linh because THAT IS THE MOST ADORABLE THING EVER. Linh is also an absolute cinnamon roll and no one can convince me otherwise. <br /><br />This series has been amazing so far and even though the love square/triangle makes it frustrating at times, the plot is amazing and the idea of the Lost Cities itself is enough to keep me hooked.<br /><br />SO THIS SERIES IS STILL AS AMAZING AS EVER AND IF YOU HADN'T READ IT, GIVE IT A GO. AS LONG AS THERE'S MORE LOVE BETWEEN BIANA AND SOPHIE I'M GOOD.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7529876662096783171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2194813503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194813503" />
    <a title="Mariam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31657573-mariam"><img alt="Mariam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601068489p2/31657573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2194813503?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariam" href="/user/show/31657573-mariam">Mariam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=2018-publication">2018-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=love-the-mc">love-the-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=best-cast">best-cast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31657573-mariam?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194813503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10334345168567111287">3 1/2 stars<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>Every time Sophie thought his name, she could hear her human parents’ voices in her mind, explaining all the reasons she should never play with fire. And yet, here she was, stepping right back into Fintan’s game.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>I couldn't sleep last night because I was thinking about the last 10% of the book so much. UGH. This book is really hard to rate; the first 50% was slow and tedious, and even though Sophie and Fitz's bonding time during this period was important (and appreciated!), it made</span>
  <span id="freeText10334345168567111287" style="display:none">3 1/2 stars<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Every time Sophie thought his name, she could hear her human parents’ voices in her mind, explaining all the reasons she should never play with fire. And yet, here she was, stepping right back into Fintan’s game.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I couldn't sleep last night because I was thinking about the last 10% of the book so much. UGH. This book is really hard to rate; the first 50% was slow and tedious, and even though Sophie and Fitz's bonding time during this period was important (and appreciated!), it made me doubt the rest of the book. <br /><br />I was wrong to ever doubt Messenger's storytelling skills.<br /><br />Yes, the first half is boring, but the second half is <i>wild</i> and introduces the heart-stopping action readers have been hoping for. The "sitting and talking" stage that took place throughout the duration of the two previous books is over, and I expect the next book to continue the fast-paced, exhilarating plot lines.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“If I fall in, you're not allowed to laugh.” <br />“I would never. I'll even give you my cape to dry off.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />What made the second half of the book far more appealing than the two previous books was the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the love triangle is finally solved! Sophitz, being canon, (unless something really bad happens) makes room for more severe problems and eases tensions between the characters. Now, Sophie and Fitz are able to focus on forwarding their relationship and dealing with their demons together. Meanwhile, Keefe and Sophie's relationship becomes more defined; their friendship reminisces of old times, and I find it suits the both of them, specifically Sophie, because she is lacking that strong, platonic bond. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Speaking of platonic bonds- where in the world were Dex and Biana? Dex has been missing through big chunks of previous books, but Biana seems to have followed suit. I hope Messenger gives her an important role to play in the next book because I believe female friendships are crucial- and without Biana, Sophie doesn't seem to have any.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i><blockquote>"What if I told you I stopped pressing buttons?" <br />"I . . . don’t know what that means."<br />"There was a moment, as the cubby was filling. Alvar was pounding on the glass, shouting things. And . . . I looked at the panel and realized one of the buttons probably opened up a drain. And I stopped pressing things."</blockquote></i><br /><br />The hive scene. The greatest scene Messenger has ever written. I'm not lying when I say I was light-headed- <i>nauseous</i>, even- when I read this. It's this specific scene that kept me up at night because this is Fitz we're talking about. Fitz, the Golden Boy; Fitz, the boy with the teal eyes and perfect smile. His anger issues have been explored in the past few books, but it really makes an appearance in <i>Flashback</i>. Although I wholeheartedly agree that these darker emotions are needed in order to make Fitz a well-defined character, I find it hard to believe how much his hatred toward Alvar has increased. As a matter of fact, I noted it to be a little too intense, although it would make sense if Alvar and Fitz's relationship previous to the betrayal were explained more.<br /><br />A few lines after this scene, Sophie is so shocked by Fitz's actions, that, despite attempting to hold his hand, she is unable to, and runs outside to Keefe. At this point, I was worried the newly created Sophie/Fitz romantic relationship was destroyed and Messenger had intended to show how Sophie was picking Keefe. However, this was not the case, and the two eventually apologized and continued supporting each other. <i>This</i> is a proper relationship, and Messenger writes it well; I am eager for what she has in store for the couple.<br /><br /><blockquote><i>"No, I’M sorry. I shouldn’t make this about me. And . . . I know there were a bunch of times yesterday when I was a total jerk and—" <br />"Don’t. It was a horrible day. No one handles situations like that perfectly. But we got through it, and now . . . we just keep going."</i></blockquote><br /><br />The ending was a little predictable, but still saddening. It works as a segue to the second "chapter" of the Sophitz relationship- Fitz choosing between Sophie or the Vacker legacy. Knowing Fitz, I have a feeling he will choose the former because he has proven himself countless times that he is loyal to those he loves. <br /><br />Sophie, on the other hand, has changed the elvin world countless times. I won't be surprised if she changes the world once more. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="10334345168567111287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2309696170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2309696170" />
    <a title="Briana Fatovic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59412023-briana-fatovic"><img alt="Briana Fatovic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517443587p2/59412023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2309696170?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briana Fatovic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briana Fatovic" href="/user/show/59412023-briana-fatovic">Briana Fatovic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481497435" href="/book/show/38364757-flashback">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59412023-briana-fatovic?shelf=books-i-read-in-2018">books-i-read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59412023-briana-fatovic?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2309696170&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2309696170" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12453599282755445052">I’m upset. This was my number one most anticipated release of the year, and I was heavily let down. The first 100 pages were a solid ⭐️⭐️⭐️. The next 600 pages ⭐️. The last 100 pages ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️. And although I really don’t like Fitz as a person, I was excited to see him have to to deal with the consequences of him “killing” Alvar. I was pumped: “Finally! A main character that has somewhat negative traits other than anger!” Alas, Alvar just had to escape; which I kind of think is a cheap shot on </span>
  <span id="freeText12453599282755445052" style="display:none">I’m upset. This was my number one most anticipated release of the year, and I was heavily let down. The first 100 pages were a solid ⭐️⭐️⭐️. The next 600 pages ⭐️. The last 100 pages ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️. And although I really don’t like Fitz as a person, I was excited to see him have to to deal with the consequences of him “killing” Alvar. I was pumped: “Finally! A main character that has somewhat negative traits other than anger!” Alas, Alvar just had to escape; which I kind of think is a cheap shot on the reader. I’m pretty over Alvar’s story line, especially since he just sucks . I believe that if Fitz was forced to face guilt over killing Alvar, he would have become a much more complex and interesting character, and a character I have stood to read about. But no, he’s innocent, as is every mother F-ING member of Sophie’s group. <br /><br />[5] Things I Hate About [Flashback]<br /><br />1. FITZPHIE: So.Much. Annoying. Romance. If you couldn’t tell, I ship Keefe and Sophie, and this book is basically a Team Foster-Keefe nightmare. The chemistry between Fitz and Sophie feels so forced. Like Fitz has no characteristics other than getting mad and being attractive.<br /><br />2. FILLER: This is very obviously a filler book. The cliffhanger at the end sets the reader up for an interesting story in book 8, but ultimately leaves book 7 to be full of nothing. There is at least 200 of Sophie in the hospital. And it was her-moping. This book was a BIG YAWN.<br /><br />3. DEX: Dex? Who’s that? I miss book one, where Dex actually got to be a part of the story. He was such a sweet cinnamon roll of a character and now he’s thrown in as a major side character. Give at least 100 pages of Fitz to Dex; he deserves it a lot more. For example, Dex possesses actual character traits. What? That’s a thing?! Because after reading this book, I’ve realized the only characters with an actual personality are Dex, Keefe, Tam, and (I guess) Sophie. So, either give me more of them, or give me character arcs DIRECTLY relating to the other characters, having nothing to do with their sibling.<br /><br />4. PERFECT CHARACTERS: Ok, I think I was reading about this in my KOTLC discord chat, but I can’t not talk about this. This kind of relates to what I talked about in the opening, but everyone in Sophie’s main group possesses no negative qualities. Absolutely. None. The characters face immense grief about stupid things that never come up in the story again after a chapter, yet after a battle where two of the Neverseen die, they’re unfazed. Someone got a scratch? WE MUST TRAIN UNTIL WE DIE. Speaking of training, it was absolutely useless. I was excited to see Sophie and her friends being badasses, but was instead greeted with hospital scenes.<br /><br />SOPHIES RESPONSE TO THIS LINE: <i>“So I just wanted to say: you don’t have to act like it’s a secret. Because it’s not. Never really has been, honestly. I’ve been waiting for you guys to figure it out for years. I am pretty sure our whole group has, between all the blushing and the cute little gifts and the ‘look at us, aren’t we the cutest cognates ever?’ and the ‘let’s stare into each other’s eyes and do some trust exercises,’ and the ‘ teal is my favorite color in the whole world but no one realizes why’ “ (676)</i><br /><br />I read this this and thought: BIG FACTS.<br /><br />What was Sophie’s response?<br /> <br /><b>“‘Wow. Okay. Not sure why you’re being such a jerk about it, but...’”</b><br /><br />Sophie.<br />ARE YOU KIDDING ME.<br /><br /><br /><br />In conclusion, Flashback was a big rip in the chat.<br /><br />4/12/20<br />hi! so as I look back at this review, I still stand by the points in which I made, but please excuse the fact that I wrote them like an angry teenager (i was one while writing this review last year )<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />2/26/18 <br />Ok so I’m still on book two and I already spoiled half the series but I just want Sophie and Keefe to be together OK?!?! And WE HAVE A DESCRIPTION<br /><br />3/12/18<br />COVER!!!!!!!!<br /><br />4/30/18<br />I was about to start this with “ok so” again, and then I realized that my writing skills having plummeted since last semester because I haven’t written an essay or anything in 5 months and I can’t pronounce anything anymore but whatever.<br /><br />Ok, enough about me. 800 PAGES. I’m shooketh. @shannon messenger, if you wanted to send me an ARC of this, I would very much appreciate #icantwaitfivemonths</span>
  <a data-text-id="12453599282755445052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2141469334" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2141469334" />
    <a title="Kaelyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64229043-kaelyn"><img alt="Kaelyn" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2141469334?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaelyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaelyn" href="/user/show/64229043-kaelyn">Kaelyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64229043-kaelyn?shelf=everyone-should-read">everyone-should-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2141469334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4728162364058484468">QUESTIONS I *NEED* TO HAVE ANSWERED IN FLASHBACK:<br/><br/>1. SHIPS. Who will Sophie end up with? Obviously Dex is out, but Keefe? Fitz? I don't think Tam is really in the running. Personally, I'm hoping for: Sophie x Keefe for sure, and Fitz x Linh. I'm still undecided about the rest of them. Part of me really really REALLY wants Dex x Biana to be a thing, but the rest of me thinks she'd be better with Tam, and plus, Tam seems like he likes her, and, um, this is Tam we're talking about here. But Tam and </span>
  <span id="freeText4728162364058484468" style="display:none">QUESTIONS I *NEED* TO HAVE ANSWERED IN FLASHBACK:<br /><br />1. SHIPS. Who will Sophie end up with? Obviously Dex is out, but Keefe? Fitz? I don't think Tam is really in the running. Personally, I'm hoping for: Sophie x Keefe for sure, and Fitz x Linh. I'm still undecided about the rest of them. Part of me really really REALLY wants Dex x Biana to be a thing, but the rest of me thinks she'd be better with Tam, and plus, Tam seems like he likes her, and, um, this is Tam we're talking about here. But Tam and Marella had kind of a "moment", if you can call it that, before they went into Nightfall #1, and Dex and Marella have basically no chemistry.<br /><br />2. SILVENY. Why is she so freaked out about Sophie visiting her? What in the world could an alicorn possibly have to do secretly? Is she, like, eating too much swizzlespice or something? Is it dangerous? Please please please let Baby Silveny be OK!!! (And also born in Flashback because the world needs another alicorn!)<br /><br />3. ALVAR. All I really need is an explanation.<br /><br />4. LADY GISELA. Why does she need Vespera's research? Why won't she let us see her face? What is her "legacy" for Keefe? What's her Archetype thing about, and what's she trying to get done?<br /><br />5. THE CACHES. What's in Fintan's cache that even he couldn't handle remembering? Also, I reeeally wanna see what's in Kenric's.<br /><br />6. KEEFE. When will Sophie figure out that he's sooo much better than Fitz in literally every way? They're "opposites attract" in literally every way. He helps her loosen up and calm down when she's tense and worried, and I honestly feel like Sophie knows Keefe better than she knows Fitz- even though she's Cognates with Fitz. Also, what emotions does he see when Sophie enhances him???<br /><br />7. SANDOR &amp; GRIZEL. When will they become a couple? Also, when will Grizel make good on her favor? 'Cause I need to see Sandor dance. Preferably with the whole gang watching.<br /><br />8. SOPHIE'S BIOLOGICAL PARENTS. Who are they? Do we know them? Also, please please please let one of them be a Vacker. Sophie and Fitz would be perfect half-siblings.<br /><br />9. SOPHIE'S ABILITIES. Please tell me there aren't more of them. Or if there are, please let them make her life harder. She's got too many as it is.<br /><br />10. SOPHIE. When will they invent glasses for romantic blindness? This is something I need to see Dex make for Sophie. Like, NOW. BEFORE she gets her matchmaking lists, please!<br /><br />UPDATE: THE BOOK IS NOW OUT AND I HAVE READ IT. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />1. SHIPS. Welp, Sophitz has become official... kinda? There has been no actual asking out, but they admitted to liking each other. Personally, I still hold out hope for Team Foster-Keefe, but we'll see where the next book takes us. No other ships yet. <br /><br />2. SILVENY. We got twins!!!!!! Wynn and Luna, who are the absolute cutest thing. Turns out the Big Scary Thing was that she was having twins and her body couldn't carry them full term- but they survived and so did the mommy!!<br /><br />3. ALVAR. Well we got an explanation... and a whole lotta drama. Alvar actually did lose his memory, and he really did think he was trying to be a good person again. Fitz didn't believe him. Turns out both of them were wrong. He agreed to be brainwashed, but only to get Neverseen people into Everglen.<br /><br />4. LADY GISELA. We still don't actually know anything. <br /><br />5. THE CACHES. They were fake. Now Keefe blames himself, and he absolutely needed more guilt in his life. Yippee.<br /><br />6. KEEFE. Speaking of... Poor guy blames himself and has blocked himself off from everyone. I'm a lil worried about him, and a lil mad at Shannon for completely ditching his characterization. I hate to say this, but (and this is a Les Mis spoiler so skip to the next bullet if you don't wanna hear) I'm a bit concerned she'll pull an Eponine on us with him. I mean obviously someone's gonna have to die, Shannon has way too many characters to make them all well-written AND there's one more guy than girl in the Sophie Gang.<br /><br />7. SANDOR &amp; GRIZEL. Pretty sure they're officially dating but no dancing yet. :(<br /><br />8. SOPHIE'S BIOLOGICAL PARENTS. No news.<br /><br />9. SOPHIE'S ABILITIES. No new ones, thank goodness. And now she has the shadowflux thingy, which makes it harder for her to do stuff. So that's good.<br /><br />10. SOPHIE. Ok so she and Fitz are now A Thing. Except she has commitment issues (understandable honey, you're only 15 after all. Take your time)... and matchmaking lists have been asked for and denied. (Here I would like to point out that Fitz's big deal breaker with dating is he can't handle a bad match... remember that.) I'm pretty sure the matchmaking issues are just because half of matchmaking is making sure you're not dating your cousin, which is a bit difficult if you can't tell the matchmakers who your biological parents are. So no biggie, it'll be resolved in a book or two... but will it be before or after Fitz breaks up with her over it and/or blows up at her for keeping the issue from her (which we all know she's gonna do. I mean, this is Sophie)? Ugh, I hate this entire relationship. It's borderline abusive at times and I don't trust Fitz any farther than I can throw him. And here's a link to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2530460613?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Madeleine's review</a> which I agree with 100% and which explains how I feel about this whole mess a lot better than I could. also her theory is terrifying but sounds pretty right.<br /><br />BONUS: TAM. Ugh this one hurts my poor heart. Tam does not deserve to be a) separated from Linh b) brainwashed by the Neverseen or c) trapped between two sides/ideas. It scares me that Lady Gisela has the fancy new soporodine (although I absolutely love her she's one of my favorite characters and so well written). We all know Tam's not gonna die cause there's a whole other love triangle around him and, as we saw in Flashback, Shannon is not opposed to abandoning plot in favor of romance. Sigh.<br /><br />FINAL VERDICT: The book was pretty poorly written, didn't answer nearly enough questions, and went completely off on the romance tangent. Also, whoever told Shannon it was a good idea to write hundreds of pages in the exact. Same. Setting. Needs to be fired. The only good news is, there's so many plot threads that have been left hanging, it's almost impossible to have this slow of a book next time around.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_2597926292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2597926292" />
    <a title="Daphne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37016646-daphne"><img alt="Daphne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592518336p2/37016646.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2597926292?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daphne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daphne" href="/user/show/37016646-daphne">Daphne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=childrens-middle-grade">childrens-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=eb">eb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37016646-daphne?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2597926292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10443991130839554199">This is the first time I've felt a bit meh about these books, which made me sad.<br/><br/>It was still a good book, entertaining and captivating as all the others, but there were a few things that made me less enthusiastic about the book than normal.<br/><br/>First of all, I think the pacing in this book wasn't very good. It started pretty well, but then after some action it dragged and dragged on for a while. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ The scenes in the hospital were tedious, and I didn't like the whole deal with the echoes.</span></span>
  <span id="freeText10443991130839554199" style="display:none">This is the first time I've felt a bit meh about these books, which made me sad.<br /><br />It was still a good book, entertaining and captivating as all the others, but there were a few things that made me less enthusiastic about the book than normal.<br /><br />First of all, I think the pacing in this book wasn't very good. It started pretty well, but then after some action it dragged and dragged on for a while. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The scenes in the hospital were tedious, and I didn't like the whole deal with the echoes. It felt kind of like the author realized she had made Elf medicine too powerful and needed to think of this very complex reason why Sophie had to stay in the hospital for a while. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Then there was also the fact that this book introduced a lot of new elements, which made it feel less cohesive and a little messy. I'm not sure how relevant this will all be in the long run, and I had a hard time getting myself to care about it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I didn't care for Sophie's new bodyguard group, and didn't really feel like the troll stuff was all that interesting, even when it came up in the story's conclusion. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />My biggest gripe is probably the romance. I've never been a fan of how it was handled in these books. There was a love square (now triangle) that Sophie seemed somewhat aware of but never really acknowledged, and even now that some stuff has started happening, she keeps seeming willfully oblivious. Not only that, but the plot keeps providing reasons why she can't just be together with one person, when it's obvious the two like each other. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I'm not particularly fond of the Sophie/Fitz ship, but then again I don't think I'm very fond of Sophie/Keefe either. I like her relationship with them both, but I prefer to explore them in a platonic way rather than focus on the crushes. That said, there's no good reason why Sophie and Fitz aren't just dating, when it's so clear they like each other and they even said so in this book. It feels to me like the author doesn't want them to get together yet, but keeps having to invent reasons to keep that from happening. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Another problem I had with this aspect of the story was that Sophie barely seemed to get any time with her friends that aren't potential love interests. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Dex is again largely missing from this book, as he seems to have disappeared a little since getting over his crush on Sophie. It's like he's not important anymore now that he's not a 'candidate' for the position of Sophie's boyfriend. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> For example, I would love to see her interact more with her female friends, or Wylie or Tam. But that barely seems to happen. <br /><br />That all said, I still did enjoy the book. For such a long book, I flew through it and really wanted to keep reading and see what was happening. But I think that's largely because I've grown invested in the characters over the past books, and not so much the plot of this particular book. I do feel sad that I now have to wait for the next one, though. I am really curious where the plot goes after this, but I hope it's a bit more focused. This book felt a little like a filler in some places, even though it did introduce a lot of new information as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10443991130839554199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39906165-sage-elizabeth?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39906165-sage-elizabeth?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39906165-sage-elizabeth?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39906165-sage-elizabeth?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1800332315" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14658045000167553465">1.) Keeper of the Lost Cities ★★★★★<br/>2.) Exile ★★★★★<br/>3.) Everblaze ★★★★★<br/>4.) Neverseen ★★★★<br/>5.) Lodestar ★★★★★<br/>6.) Nightfall ★★★★★<br/>6.1.) Nightfall: Keefe Short Story ★★★★★<br/><br/>WE KNOW THE PLOT<br/>SORT KF<br/>WHO IS GOING TO FACE A DANGER<br/>WHAT IS WORSE THAN THE NEVERSEEN<br/>WHAT MERMORIES<br/>WILL WE FIND OUT HER PARENTS<br/>I<br/>NEED<br/>THIS<br/>NOW<br/><br/><br/>FLASHBACK<br/>WAIT WJDBSJX<br/>OK BREATHE SAGE<br/>BrEAtHe sAGe</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2735675457" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2735675457" />
    <a title="Aqua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44266986-aqua"><img alt="Aqua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502852541p2/44266986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2735675457?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aqua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aqua" href="/user/show/44266986-aqua">Aqua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481497435" href="/book/show/38364757-flashback">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44266986-aqua?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44266986-aqua?shelf=why-did-i-read-this-crap">why-did-i-read-this-crap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44266986-aqua?shelf=guilty-pleasure-books">guilty-pleasure-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735675457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1934852419750653642">Well, this series has hit a new low. <i>Flashback</i> removes everything that was still entertaining about this series and instead gives us endless discussions of logistics, medical treatments, and more Fitzphie than I can handle.<br/><br/><b>So. Much. Boring. Filler.</b><br/>Have you ever wanted to read an extensive novel about a character in a hospital stay that details every mundane detail of their treatment? No? Me neither! And yet, early on in <i>Flashback</i>, Sophie and Fitz get injured and have to stay in the hospital wing</span>
  <span id="freeText1934852419750653642" style="display:none">Well, this series has hit a new low. <i>Flashback</i> removes everything that was still entertaining about this series and instead gives us endless discussions of logistics, medical treatments, and more Fitzphie than I can handle.<br /><br /><b>So. Much. Boring. Filler.</b><br />Have you ever wanted to read an extensive novel about a character in a hospital stay that details every mundane detail of their treatment? No? Me neither! And yet, early on in <i>Flashback</i>, Sophie and Fitz get injured and have to stay in the hospital wing (or whatever it's called in this series) at Foxfire for an extended period of time. To be specific, they spend 8hrs and 40 min of the 23hr and 9min long audiobook in the hospital. That is 37.5% of this 848 page book. <b>37.5% of a book late in the series not accomplishing anything.</b> <br /><br />Instead of plot progression or character development for any of the long-neglected side characters, we are graced with endless descriptions of injuries and treatments and Sophie and Fitz being disgustingly mushy. After they finally get out, we shift to endless bodyguard logistics discussions. Why? <i>WHY?!</i> Why waste hundreds of pages on nothing? Why not just fast forward through the hospital stay? And why are we wasting time talking about more bodyguards when we all <i>know</i> they won't be able to protect Sophie? She will obviously have to face the Neverseen again because plot (or lack there of). <br /><br /><b>Everyone but Sophie and Fitz get the shaft in this book.</b> All the wonderful side characters are almost completely absent until the final fight, and in its place we get the Neverending Fitzphie Show. When anyone else is actually present, they are reduced to commenting on the love triangle. Why can't Tam, Linh, Marella, Wylie, Dex, and Biana have their own side plots and character development? Why can't we ever see Sophie interact with people who aren't love interests? Can anyone talk about anything other than who Sophie's dating? Even Keefe, the shining light of this series, is written out of most of this novel in the stupidest way.<br /><br /><b>Fitz has somehow become an even more terrible character.</b> Fitz, who has managed to be incredibly perfect and boring this entire series, has doubled down hard on his one defining character trait: anger. This character has had some serious anger management issues since book 2, and though we saw some resurgence of it towards Keefe back during his Neverseen days, it has come back in full force in this book. <i>And yet everyone just hand waves it away!</i> Remember how much grief everyone gave Keefe for being reckless? None of that for perfect boy Fitz. Let's take a look at a couple excerpts, shall we? <blockquote><i>Fitz whipped around. "So then you guys knew this was happening?"<br />"Fitz..." Della tried. <br />He shook his head, turning to Sophie and Keefe. "Did you know too? Is that why you're here?"<br />-----------------------------<br />"If we didn't let them use Everglen, they would've found somewhere else."<br />"Fine by me!" Fitz shouted. <br />"I dunno," Keefe jumped in. "Wouldn't you rather be able to keep an eye on Alvar?"<br />Fitz reeled on him. "You're on </i>their<i> side? Is that why you just sat there and talked about your stupid hair?"<br />"Okay, first? We both know my hair is awesome," Keefe said with his hugest smirk yet. "And second: it's not like they're setting your brother free. Were you listening to Dizznee? I'm pretty sure if Alvar breathes too hard, Dex'll zap him."<br />"Don't even get me started on Dex," Fitz muttered.<br />"I know," Biana said quietly. "I can't believe he knew for a week and didn't tell us."<br />Sophie opened her mouth to defend Dex but swallowed back the words. She could tell Fitz and Biana weren't ready to hear them. <br />Fitz must've noticed, though, because he reeled toward her. "Don't tell me you're okay with this."<br />"'Okay' isn't the right word," she mumbled. "I think... it's a hard call."<br />"A hard call," Fitz repeated. "That's it? I thought for </i>this<i> of all things, we'd be on the same side."<br />"We are," Sophie promised, reaching for him. <br />He jerked away. "No, we're--"<br />Keefe stepped between them......<br />-----------------------------<br />"It's killing them you know," Biana said quietly. "Knowing you're here, still recovering, and don't want to see them. I catch mom crying all the time."<br />"Good," Fitz said.<br />"Don't be like that," she told him. <br />"And don't tell me you're on </i>their<i> side now!"</i></blockquote> Wow, what a guy. He lashes out at his parents, his sister, his supposed best friend, and even Sophie, accusing them all of withholding information and taking sides when the situation is clearly more complex than that. Sophie just forgives him as usual. Lashing out is clearly a great start to a relationship. But I guess being a cute boy makes everything ok. Except sadly, it often does in the real world. And we are supposed to <i>like</i> this character?<br /><br />I also find it weird how often we are told Fitz and Keefe are best friends, because I cannot remember <i>ever</i> seeing Fitz act like it. He lashes out at Keefe <i>a lot</i>, and refused to give him the benefit of the doubt throughout the entirety of his time in the Neverseen. <br /><br />Let's also not forget Fitz has been repeatedly pressuring Sophie to sign up for the match, and implied he wouldn't date her if she didn't because he didn't want to be in a bad match. Yeah... Can you feel the love?<br /><br /><b>Still no sign of any plot progression.</b> I'm not even sure if the author knows where this series is supposed to go anymore. What has been the point of the last 4 books? There's a scene early on where Keefe goes over all the stuff they don't know about the Neverseen, which is basically everything. And then the author even reverses one of the Black Swan's only accomplishments of the last 4 books. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Making the caches fake was incredibly unnecessary and infuriating. What was even the point of the entire story arc of Keefe joining the Neverseen for anyway? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> How can this be book 7/9 (or possibly 10 as I have recently heard)? <br /><br /><b>I'm starting to get <i>really</i> sick of the Neverseen outsmarting everyone.</b> This goes way beyond your standard making-your-villains-clever-to-make-the-good-guys-underdogs stuff. The Neverseen literally know everything the good guys are going to do. Everytime. Conflict scenes are not even suspenseful anymore. Because I know the Neverseen have predicted everything that will happen and it will be revealed they manipulated Sophie and Co. the whole time and this was all part of their plan, etc., etc. Since every scene of the good guys "winning" has been reversed to be all part of the evil plan all along, what does it even matter anymore. <br /><br /><b>Looking back the plot of every book has basically been:</b><br />1) Sophie and Co. investigate Neverseen stuff. <br />2) Obnoxious love triangle nonsense ensues.<br />3) All interesting side characters get to do nothing. <br />4) Sophie and Co. discuss the most recently introduced convoluted plot point. <br />5) Hundreds of pages of filler ensue.<br />6) Sophie and Co. confront the Neverseen. <br />7) Everything was part of the Neverseen's plan all along because they predicted everything ever. <br />8) Sophie and/or one other friend gets injured, but they all escape because plot armor.<br />9) We learn nothing of the Neverseen's goals. The End.<br /><br />I'm sorry, but this is just not gonna fly anymore. <i>We are 3/4 of the way into this series (supposedly)!</i> This series needs to get its act together and start building towards something. Or completing character arcs. Or making an actual point. Or resolving the many unresolved mysteries. Or <i>something</i>. How many more books is it going to take? <br /><br /><b>So much convoluted detail!</b> It seems like the author has gotten lost in details. Details can be great, but not at the expense of the plot. Which is weird, because despite the fact these characters talk about almost nothing but the plot, we have still gotten nowhere. Instead we have to talk about the 73rd jewelry gadget Sophie has acquired, or the endless, stupid love triangle, or a million what-ifs about the Neverseen's plans, or Sophie freaking out, or the latest addition to the mess of convolution, shadow flux. Yep. As if there weren't enough stupid random convoluted things our heroes have to deal with, something called shadow flux is introduced here, and you will hear <i>a lot</i> about it. Far more than you will ever hear about the Neverseen's motivations, or character development for all the side characters, or the good guys actually accomplishing something. <br /><br /><b>It's Spoiler Time!</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>Nothing is accomplished. What a shock.</b> To no one's surprise, nothing of note is accomplished in <i>Flashback</i>, except another member of the Neverseen is conveniently killed by accident (not through our heroes' wits, of which they have none). I'm disappointed. Umber was really built up in this book, and she didn't really do much at all before being snuffed out. <br /><br />Even after all Sophie talks big about <i>this time</i> being the time they will be prepared, and <i>this time</i> they will fight back, and <i>this time</i> they will win and blah blah, Sophie and Co. are once again outwitted by the Neverseen and get captured almost instantly. The bodyguards are once again basically useless. Sophie literally falls into every trap the Neverseen set, <b>yet again</b>.<blockquote><i>This time, Lady Gisela beat them.</i></blockquote> She beats you <i>every time</i>. <b>EVERY TIME!!!</b> Will these heroes ever be even the least bit competent? Will the plot ever progress? What is even the point of these books anymore? Is the author going for the world record on number of pages that accomplish nothing? <br /><br /><b>Alright, let's talk about Fitz again.</b> I hate Fitz. I have always hated his character and after this book I now REALLY hate him. He does at least finally get some character development related to his anger management. Here are a few more excerpts: <blockquote><i>Biana looked convinced, especially when Keefe told him, "He's telling the truth. I'd be able to tell if he wasn't." Fitz snorted. "Right - like you could tell with your mom." Which was a super low blow.<br />-----------------------------<br />Fitz had his arm pressed to Alvar's throat. Cutting off his air supply. "TELL ME WHAT YOU WERE DOING OUT HERE!" he demanded ...... When neither of them seemed to get through to him, Sophie stepped closer, whispering in Fitz's ear, "You have to be careful of your echo."<br />-----------------------------<br />Before Dex could answer, Fitz let out a frustrated growl and yanked the bracelet off his wrist, flinging it into the darkness as hard as he could.<br />-----------------------------<br />But when she told Fitz that Keefe also thought he should wait, Fitz's mental voice sharpened. "Well that's convenient."<br />"What is?" she asked.<br />"Keefe siding with you. I wonder why he'd do that."<br />-----------------------------<br />"There was a moment, as the cubby was filling. Alvar was pounding on the glass, shouting things. And... I looked at the panel and realized one of the buttons probably opened up a drain. And I stopped pressing things." Sophie's mouth went dry with the confession, and her insides twisted all kinds of horrible ways. But, she knew what he needed ...... "Life is series of hard choices."</i></blockquote> Wow there's a lot to unpack here. Fitz getting unreasonably jealous of Keefe, Fitz showing violent tendencies, Fitz showing a desire to hurt people before they do anything wrong, and yep... Fitz murdered his brother. And doesn't regret it. Real likable guy right here. <br /><br />Sophie is frustratingly calm in reacting to Fitz's anger issues. These are some extreme red flags about his character. When he literally nearly murders Alvar, she's just like "oh, be careful of your echo, sweetie." She actually apologizes to him at one point. She APOLOGIZES when she did nothing wrong! This has some serious abusive relationship red flags. I am horrified that the author is not analyzing this. This is middle-grade for goodness sake. After Fitz actually murders Alvar, she just says "life choices are hard." ARE YOU KIDDING ME?! <i>Finally,</i> after the life choices comment she gets understandably freaked out by him and runs into Keefe's arms. But if I thought that would be the end of the horrible love triangle plot, then... well I guess I shouldn't be surprised anymore. There was a minute I thought Keefe and Sophie would discuss it. Or at least Sophie and Fitz might. But nope! After <i>ALL THAT</i> Sophie just carries on like nothing has changed between her and Fitz and she's still in love with him? Really? <i>REALLY?!</i> <b>Are you fucking kidding me?</b> <br /><br />Oh but PSYCH! Alvar is alive and escapes because no one dies in this series except unimportant characters. But alive or not, let's not forget Fitz did not just contemplate, but <i>attempted</i> to murder someone. <i>And didn't regret it.</i> We're not going to analyze this at all? Just right back to Fitzphie blushes and giggles? I want to vomit. <br /><br /><b>Sophie still has these random moments when she turns into a complete unlikeable asshole.</b> She still gets jealous anytime Fitz and Linh are even in the same room. And then there is this scene: <blockquote><i>Sophie glanced at Fitz, wishing they were trusting people she actually liked. But they'd lost enough time. "Okay," she said. "Let's go." Under different circumstances, Sophie might've enjoyed how much the Hekses flailed and screamed when she made them plummet into the void - or the way they landed in a heap among the grassy dunes.</i></blockquote> Geez. Sophie apparently enjoys scaring people she doesn't like. Even though the Hekses never actually did anything except not love her like the rest of the world does.<br /><br />Her obnoxious self-importance is in full view not much later as well, when she is throwing her weight around in front of all the veterinary experts, hysterically insisting they are not trying hard enough and that there must be a way to save Silveny's babies just because she wants there to be. Even though all the experts <i>are</i> doing all they can. Clearly the calm-mindedness one would hope for in a leader. <br /><br />On an unrelated note, I was pissed Keefe wasn't present for the whole Silveny incident. He is the character who was with Sophie for all of the Silveny stuff thus far, it seems a bit unfair to not let him take part in helping her after all that, just so we can have stupid Fitzphie be alone. <br /><br />But since nothing sad is ever permanent in this series, Tarina pulls a deus ex machina out of her butt.<br /><br /><b>Poor Tam.</b> Because this series is determined to accomplish nothing and reverse any accomplishments that actually occur (ie. the fake caches reveal that destroyed Keefe's character arc), apparently we now have to watch Tam go through <i>literally</i> the same character arc Keefe just went through. Are you kidding me? One angsty-good-guy-joins-the-bad-guys arc is enough for a series, thank you very much. And now I'm sure we're now going to have to waste the whole of the next book to wrap up this Tam plotline.<br /><br />I wanted Tam to get some of his own character development, sure, but not the same character development as Keefe! And despite all the talking to Vespera and Gisela, you'll never guess what we still don't know about. <blockquote><i>"The day will come when you'll finally understand what we're truly working toward..."</i></blockquote>Can that day come now? <br /><br />Yep. That's right. After 7 books, <b>SEVEN BOOKS</b>, we <i>still don't know what they Neverseen's plans are</i>. *flips table*<br /><br /><b>The Match</b><br />Really? After all the pain the Match has caused Jolie and Dex's parents, Sophie just registers for the Match anyway? Just like that? Because Fitz gives you flutters, we're giving up on all our morals and any attempt to make a point with these books? <br /><br /><b>Random Thoughts</b><br />---"Keeping track of dates in the lost cities was impossible." ...Tell me about it. <br />---Best quote of this book: "Why do clothes never have enough pockets? There should always be lots of pockets."<br />---Do these elves eat anything other than sugary sweets? <br />---Sophie learns to throw daggers in 30 min? Really? <i>Really?</i><br />---Seems kind of hypocritical and racist (species-ist?) that the elves talk about ogres/goblins kissing as something "gross." Maybe the ogres and goblins are sick of watching the will-they-won't-they nonsense going on with Sophie? I know I am.<br />---Not a fan of how a normal thing like birth is treated as something disgusting by Sophie. <br />---I'm getting a bit tired of how all powerful Ruy is.<br />---No one assumed the villains would notice them training with weapons in plain sight?<br />---How do the trolls keep the newborns from murdering each other?<br />---Isn't it pathetic that human fingerprint sensors are more secure than the stupid elves' DNA sensors that apparently open to any trace of someone's very easily stealable DNA?<br />---Marella gets shafted as expected, just like Tam, Linh, Biana, Dex, and Wylie. Despite her manifesting as a pyrokinetic being a plot development with huge potential. <br />---For all the powers Super Special Snowflake Sophie has, she doesn't use them much. Or effectively.<br />---Freaking horrible love triangle has hijacked the plot. No one likes love triangles. <br /><br /><b>Keefe is 100% right that the Alvar-opens-the-gate plan was long-winded, convoluted, and could have been accomplished much easier. What a great analogy for this series.</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>Flashback</i> is my new least favorite book in this series. I honestly can't think of anything I liked about this book. Which is sad, because every book so far has at least had some parts I enjoyed. This book had some huge pacing problems, and that is saying something for this series. I still think overall this series is ~2.5 stars, and I would've given this book 2 stars, if only for Keefe and my other favorite side characters occasionally making a cameo, but I'm subtracting another for her not analyzing Fitz's actions. First the gnome slavery thing and now this. I don't know right now if I can stand to keep going unless she reverses the Fitzphie stuff. Not analyzing the potentially abusive tendencies of Fitz is downright dangerous. <br /><br /><b>What this series needs</b><br />I still think this series has potential to be decent, but it has increasingly focused on the worst aspects of itself over the past few books. This is what needs to happen to get this shit back on track: <br />---Have Sophie stop hand waving Fitz's anger issues and realize that Fitz lashing out, accusing her of taking sides, pressuring her into the match, acting extremely jealous, showing violent tendencies, etc is not healthy or normal relationship behavior. And no amount of cute boy can make it ok. This is extremely horrifying to me, seeing how often these traits are rationalized in real life. It doesn't matter that he's sweet sometimes. Manipulative behavior intermixed with sweetness is textbook abusive relationship. Please don't let this stand, please back pedal on this plot.<br />---Just end the horrible love triangle already. No one likes love triangles.<br />---Let all the wonderful side characters have character development and let them talk about things other than the love triangle or the Neverseen.<br />---Pick up the pacing A LOT. Start solving mysteries, have our heroes accomplish something, stop reversing deaths. We are 7 books in. It's time to build to the finale.<br />---Stop shuffling the villains and tell us what the Neverseen's goals are. PLEASE.<br />---Decide on your message and stick to it. Is the message prejudice is bad? Then make sending this message a priority.<br />---Be aware of the real world implications of your writing when you get into topics like slavery, racism, abusive relationships, abortion, science, vaccines, etc. <br /><br />Can this series still be salvaged? I don't know. But I'm not super hopeful right now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1934852419750653642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2322891440" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2322891440" />
    <a title="Mya Gray" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76956135-mya-gray"><img alt="Mya Gray" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593285995p2/76956135.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2322891440?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mya Gray" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mya Gray" href="/user/show/76956135-mya-gray">Mya Gray</a>
