<div id="review_2233853546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2233853546" />
    <a title="Castles of Air" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19333526-castles-of-air"><img alt="Castles of Air" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528324905p2/19333526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2233853546?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Castles of Air" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Castles of Air" href="/user/show/19333526-castles-of-air">Castles of Air</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2233853546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2399952609017777864">❋❋❋❋❋❋❋<i>
  <b>Spoilers for books 1-6 (all of the books before this one) below the cut</b>
</i>❋❋❋❋❋❋❋<br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/><i>Update</i> ➜ <b>March 25, 2018</b><br/><br/>We now have a cover!!!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1520545883l/32762937.jpg' width='400' height='600' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So obviously, we have Tam, Sophie, and Wylie. Or maybe Prentence? I'm feeling it's probably Wylie, though. He really looks similar to his picture in the official art. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522004731i/25273646._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='600' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>They are all wearing cloaks that are white underneath and black on top. Sophie's cloak has a pin with what appears to be wings holding it together. I'm not sure if that's a reference t</span></span>
  <span id="freeText2399952609017777864" style="display:none">❋❋❋❋❋❋❋<i>
  <b>Spoilers for books 1-6 (all of the books before this one) below the cut</b>
</i>❋❋❋❋❋❋❋<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><i>Update</i> ➜ <b>March 25, 2018</b><br><br>We now have a cover!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1520545883l/32762937.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So obviously, we have Tam, Sophie, and Wylie. Or maybe Prentence? I'm feeling it's probably Wylie, though. He really looks similar to his picture in the official art. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522004731i/25273646._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They are all wearing cloaks that are white underneath and black on top. Sophie's cloak has a pin with what appears to be wings holding it together. I'm not sure if that's a reference to anything we know of yet so far. Sophie is wearing her gloves and a purple dress, and is throwing what I believe to be a ninja star. I don't see anything else that seems to be distinctive about their outfits. <br><br>Tam appears to be shadowcasting (the best word I can think of for what they are doing, I'm not really sure) with Wylie. Wylie is a Flasher, so I guess it would make sense that he would be able to work with Tam. I think whatever they are casting is causing the image of the stairway to appear. I think the forest is separate from the image with the stairs, maybe they are creating some kind of portal there? I think the stairs place may be the same as the ones they went up before (I am terrible with names, I should really look this up), the ones where Fitz let Sophie throw his brother's award off of. However, I don't believe those had railings on them, so maybe not. I also don't really have many ideas of where the forest may be. It doesn't seem particularly distinctive.<br><br>Interestingly, if you think about the staircase image as a portal to the forest and think about how Sophie appears to be coming out of it, the placement of Tam and who I guess to be Wylie doesn't make sense, unless you consider that Tam and Wylie were already at the forest and made the portal for Sophie to come through. We have seen Tam trigger the opening of a portal, or at least make the appearance of one known before, so I guess it isn't completely out of the realm of possibility. And we did hear some vague mentionings of the Vacker's ancient relative, Fallon Vacker, who could possibly be a Flasher like another one of their relatives, Orem Vacker. <br><br><i>Update</i> ➜ <b>February 20, 2018</b><br><br>This is it guys, we have a teasing title and the cover is soon to follow - who do you think will be on the cover? I'm going to place my bets on Keefe, Sophie, and Fitz.<br><br>We also have some info from Shannon (which is a relief!)<br><br><blockquote>WE HAVE A TITLE!!!!!!!!<br><br>Cover and plot description to come later (and no, I don't know when)--but just so we're clear:<br><br>WHAT THE TITLE *DOES* MEAN: Memory plays a BIG role in book 7 (which you can probably guess from certain things that happened in NIGHTFALL--please don't spoil)<br><br>WHAT THE TITLE DOES *NOT* MEAN: The entire book is one long flashback. Mind you, it'd be fun to mess with you guys that way, but even I'm not *that* evil. 🤣 (this is also not a prequel. this is the seventh book, and a continuation of everything. Calling it flashback will make sense when you read)</blockquote>
<br><br>Sidenote, it just occurred to me that Psychic/Livie was also (probably?) in the Black Swan before Sophie was born. So we can add that to the list of possible suspects: Squall/Mrs. Diznee, Wraith, and Blur. I think it would be pretty cool if Squall was Sophie's mother because then Sophie would also be biologically related to Edaline (because Mrs. Diznee is her sister). Although, that might make things between Sophie and Dex quite awkward. (Watch, the book will end right before we learn who her real parents are - Shannon please do not do that!)<br><br><i>Update</i> ➜ <b>December 30, 2017:</b><br><br>I say it many times, that I hate people who review unreleased books, but I allow myself this one exception because Shannon Messenger never fails to deliver. My excitement is definitely a 5/5 stars!<br><br>Among the many unanswered questions: (spoilers for all previous books, of course)<br><br>1. <i>Why is Lady Gisela hiding her face?</i> Obviously, she most likely has gruesome scars, but I intensely suspect that there is some deeper motivation.<br><br>2. <i>Silveny's panic</i>. Why was she so panicked and secretive that one time when Sophie tried to contact her? I know this has kind of drifted to the back burner in light of some more....<i>immenent</i> issues, but it still remains a mystery unsolved. <br><br>3. <i>Sophie's biological parents.</i> We've been teased at this since basically the beginning of the series. I know its probably being withheld until it is significant to the current state of the plot but I REALLY NEED TO KNOW OKAY!! We do know that her parents don't know who the other parent is. And its pretty much confirmed that it isn't Kenric, Jolie, Tiergan, Prentence, and Mr. Forkle (I think but I don't 100% remember??). They were probably in the Black Swan at the time of her....creation, I guess you could call it. So far, of characters we know, that includes Squall/Mrs. Diznee and whoever Blur is. Also, he did mention that Enhancer was naturally a part of her genome and he decided to keep it, so maybe she's related to a character with that ability. <br><br>4. <i>Sophie's other abilities</i>. So far we've got Telepath, Enhancer, Polygot, Teleporter, and Inflictor. We also know that it most likely isn't something extremely volatile, like Pyrokinetic. It sounds like she does have at least one other ability, from Mr. Forkle's cryptic answer to her when she asked. <br><br>5. <i>Alavar</i>. I don't really know what else to say about this. It's almost completely certain that he isn't faking his memory loss, so what/who caused it, and why exactly did they decide to leave him for dead? Can his memories be triggered or are they gone forever? And this will definitely be a difficult situation to deal with in this next book. Is it morally acceptable to punish someone for something that they don't remember? Will he be just as manipulative and awful without his memories, meaning that his terrible person tendencies are deeply embedded in his character, or will he be different without them?<br><br>6. <i>What is in the caches?</i> Its nigh time that we get at least one thing out of those darn caches that were so hard won. Obviously, there will be information about Vespera.<br><br>7. <i>Prentence.</i> GUYS, THIS IS IT, HE'S FINALLY HEALED!!! But.....of course, it's complicated. Will he return to himself to be able to tell the Black Swan about what exactly happened before his arrest and mind break? Will he even be able to deal with his wife's death, son's torture, and all of their lost years? <br><br>8. <i>Vespera</i> What is the intent of her experiments, and why was Gisela so interested in them? I've wanted to punch her in the face for being such a stubborn pain in the butt for most of the book and I know I'm not alone in that. We do know it has something to do with human emotions and the capacity for violence so it already sounds quite unpleasant. Also, how does Fallon Vacker factor into this?<br><br>9. <i>Biana</i>. I know she's going to survive, but how will this change her personality and the group's chemistry as a result? Also, I'm hella proud of her. And Linh. And Tam. And Dex. And Fitz. And yes, even Keefe. <br><br>10. <i>Keefe in general</i>. Will we find out why he is so in tuned with Sophie's emotions in particular? And the rest of his hidden memories? And his "legacy"? Gisela made some loose references to what it actually may be but I don't really think its as simple as being Nightfall (either one of them) or a book or something. It seems to carry a lot more weight than even that.<br><br>11.<i>What is Fintan's plan?</i> Of course, it is never really what's expected. We can't really get an idea at the moment, and even if we did it would probably be wrong I'm guessing. <br><br>12. <i>Marella's secret.</i> Will this become public now, because of the events at Nightfall? And what will that do to her? Is there hope for progress with the Pyrokinetic ability? I mean, tbh, trying to making people with a dangerous, hard to control ability just ignore it sounds like a recipe for disaster to me personally, at least try to teach them to control it at the very least. It seems as though Bronte will be accepting at the very least, as he already knows about it. Also, there was a tease at what happened to Marella's mom as far as her sanity goes, and it seems that she was involved with the Black Swan in some way before it happened?<br><br>13. <i>Will Sandor x Grizel happen?</i> I really hope it does. Speaking of which, Sophie owes Fitz a dance as well as Sandor owes Grizel one, so dance party in the near future?<br><br>14. <i>Fitzphie or Keephie?</i> The romantic tension has definitely been rising, between the Dezphie incident, Fitz's very frequent gifts, and Ftiz's determination to find out what her secret is. Personally, I think both Keefe and Fitz have feelings for Sophie, and Sophie has an intense crush on Fitz and doesn't exactly know what to feel about Keefe. Sidenote, Biana most likely has a crush on Keefe. Or Dex?? Idk this is confusing. Maybe even Tamphie might be a thing?? Who knows, I have a feeling things are about to get very romantically interesting in the next book.<br><br>15. <i>Will this be the last book?</i> I'm assuming the "confirmed another 2 books" includes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762917.Nightfall__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__6_" title="Nightfall (Keeper of the Lost Cities #6) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightfall</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762937.Flashback__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___7_" title="Flashback (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #7) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Untitled</a>, so could this be the last book? And if not, I assume there will be one more book after this and no more. I don't want to think about that. HOWEVER, there is a lot of room for spin-offs in this universe, because let's face it, there are still so many unanswered questions about the very rich universe of these books and their characters that could definitely be answered and expanded upon.<br><br>16. <i>Damel</i> I like the guy's personality, but something about him just feels <i>off</i>. I think it was one of his comments about a past wash he has done although I don't completely remember. But I am suspcious. We do know the Neverseen have a Telepath, and presumably a Telepath trained in washing. Connection? Maybe. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2399952609017777864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1796540454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1796540454" />
    <a title=" Lorien Rhys ~ Live for tomorrow " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow"><img alt=" Lorien Rhys ~ Live for tomorrow " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600123078p2/56477241.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1796540454?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Lorien Rhys ~ Live for tomorrow " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Lorien Rhys ~ Live for tomorrow " href="/user/show/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow"> Lorien Rhys ~ Live for tomorrow </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=favorites-in-2018">favorites-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=elves">elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=lord-of-the-rings-related">lord-of-the-rings-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=visually-stunning">visually-stunning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=mc-female">mc-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=abilities">abilities</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56477241-lorien-rhys-live-for-tomorrow?shelf=need-to-read-now">need-to-read-now</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1796540454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer844010219241439953">Quite honestly, I enjoyed Flashback LOADS better than Nightfall. The characters were actually busy doing something instead of standing around and twiddling their thumbs and doing absolutely nothing of importance. Really, most of the content in Nightfall could be taken out and it wouldn’t affect the story. Number one rule of writing (as deemed by my peers): if you write a scene and it won’t affect the story, take it out. That, my dears, is what you call a filler. (If I am wrong, please tell me) A</span>
  <span id="freeText844010219241439953" style="display:none">Quite honestly, I enjoyed Flashback LOADS better than Nightfall. The characters were actually busy doing something instead of standing around and twiddling their thumbs and doing absolutely nothing of importance. Really, most of the content in Nightfall could be taken out and it wouldn’t affect the story. Number one rule of writing (as deemed by my peers): if you write a scene and it won’t affect the story, take it out. That, my dears, is what you call a filler. (If I am wrong, please tell me) And yes, though I found it painful that  some 300+ pages (or is it 400....), the story was interesting. Now, here comes the doom train.<br><br><i>The stinkin VACKER LEGACY</i><br>Well to start off with, the “VACKER LEGACY” has always been thought of as very sinister, at least that’s how Alvar described it in Neverseen. But I was really disappointed when the “VACKER LEGACY”, this legacy that we were all curious about, turned out to be about a secret <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[HIVE IN EVERGLEN THAT LUZIA VACKER HID FOR WHATEVER REASON <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542818696ra/26629986.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This big reveal of the “VACKER LEGACY” was seriously so disappointing you have no idea. Now, if Mrs. Messenger were to add a few more secrets of the “VACKER LEGACY”, THAT would be VERY appealing. I just hope she doesn’t build up all this tension of the “VACKER LEGACY” for nothing. <br><br><i>Neverseen</i><br>Okay. When you have a insane group, you should probably live up to those standards. Not just attack our beloved heroes with slithery shadow powers. Yes. That scene at the beginning was very terrifying and I actually thought a few important characters were going to actually DIE i.e. Dex. But later on, the Neverseen never pose a HUGE threat. Other than being the ones to reveal the “VACKER LEGACY”. They weren’t even worth dwelling over because they really showed up once and another time, and that was it. They weren’t the evil maniacs we knew them to be throughout the series. The Neverseen was just in the book.... to be in the book. Sure, they played a part with Alvar, but it was his decision in the beginning. I get it, it may have to do with the fact that elves can’t handle violence, but wouldn’t the Neverseen have figured out a way to move around that? Otherwise, why even bother be the crazy group? I dunno, but the series seems to be going downhill? Don’t get me wrong, I enjoy it just as much as the next person, but there’s just something about this whole series that I can’t put my finger on.<br><br><i>Fitz</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542818696ra/26629985.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Man, oh man. We really need to work on your anger issues. I get it, you’re mad at your brother, but don’t be always known as that one rager kid in a series. -_- It’s just painful for 99% of us Keeper fans. Especially when some of us want to support you with Sophie but man, your attitude... Yes, I’m sure most of you are probably praising the Lord right now. As much as it hurts my soul, Fitz just isn’t a good character. I should’ve realized this in Exile, but I thought that maybe things would be better and he would actually GROW. But nope. He hasn’t. And his anger issues are just as ferocious as in Exile. The only characters that develop in a good way is Dex and Keefe. Yes. Not the Mary Sue Sophie but them. They are the most precious characters in the series and why Sophie didn’t have the brains to be closer to them, is a mystery. Even when Keefe actually shows his affection, not through trinkets and gifts, Sophie seems to appreciate the gifts (Fitz) than the way Keefe cares for her. Yeesh. I’m getting too mushy over here.<br><br><i>Last minute thoughts</i><br>If you were to not read Nightfall and dropped right into Flashback, you wouldn’t miss a thing. Yes. The Alvar situation is kind of crucial, but it’s that important. Most of Nightfall doesn’t even matter, in case that wasn’t clear before. Especially when our dear ol’ Sophie never seems to actually develop. Yeah she convinces Sandor to give her battle training but yipeedeedado. Our MC wants to throwing ninja stars at enemies.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542818696ra/26629984.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Whoo! You show them Sophie! I really couldn’t feel more sorry for a character than Sophie. She’s fifteen, finally confirmed in Flashback, but she still acts and thinks like she’s twelve. Honestly, Sophie isn’t growing, she’s just. . . agh. She’s a pain and a terrible character for us to read. Let’s all be honest, we’d rather be reading about Keefe than Sophie.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542818408ra/26629955.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let’s not deny it. Keefe is just more compelling than Sophie. He goes through struggles that matter for the plot. If Mrs. Messenger actually switched the POV to Keefe, I wouldn’t be upset. Sophie is just stale. Keefe is vibrant and alive. <br><br>Thank you for your attention. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542818321ra/26629952.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2588901297" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2588901297" />
    <a title="Briana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5984479-briana"><img alt="Briana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559064864p2/5984479.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2588901297?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briana" href="/user/show/5984479-briana">Briana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5984479-briana?shelf=broken-records">broken-records</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2588901297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4237756995936296117">"Plus, Grizel and Ro wanted them to master swords and knives and all kinds of other stabby things."<br/><br/>"...but I think we should carry them with us to save time, so...we'll need pockets. Why do clothes never have enough pockets? There should always be lots of pockets...the more pockets the better!"<br/><br/>"And don't look so nervous, Foster. Trust the foot energy!"<br/>"I've never used foot energy!"<br/>"Eh, you've always been a fast learner."<br/>Elwin joined them from his office.<br/>"You're going to tell us we can't do this,</span>
  <span id="freeText4237756995936296117" style="display:none">"Plus, Grizel and Ro wanted them to master swords and knives and all kinds of other stabby things."<br /><br />"...but I think we should carry them with us to save time, so...we'll need pockets. Why do clothes never have enough pockets? There should always be lots of pockets...the more pockets the better!"<br /><br />"And don't look so nervous, Foster. Trust the foot energy!"<br />"I've never used foot energy!"<br />"Eh, you've always been a fast learner."<br />Elwin joined them from his office.<br />"You're going to tell us we can't do this, right?" she asked. "Because it'll hurt my recovery?"<br />"Nah. I just want to see what happens."<br /><br />"Battles are not for heroics, contrary to what many foolishly believe. They're for winning. That must always be your overall goal. If you manage to save anyone in the process, that's a bonus. But your endgame must be victory."<br /><br /><br /><br />I became very worried about reading this installment when I realized the synopsis was extremely vague and had no specifics to tie in from the last book. You could apply it to any of the last three books and it would still work with the plots. From the size of this book, I was hoping for more action, secrets revealed by the Black Swan (who except for a few introductions and sporadic comings and goings, we don't really interact with them), or even some hidden insight into the Neverseen's plan. Instead, we got more of a trip to the hospital for half the book, then the recovery process, then a lot of what-ifs about the Neverseen. At this point, it feels like we're not going to be getting any reveals about the Neverseen or the Black Swan in any substantial quality that would help with many of the questions, the main one being why are they doing this and for what purpose??????<br /><br />I never really picked a side in the romantic aspect of this series, but after the disaster with Fitz when his father's mind shattered and the awful things Fitz said to Sophie, I've only been able to see him as the already announced love interest who doesn't have to try to get the girl cause it's been predetermined already. That being said, this book really pushed me over to liking Keefe more as a love interest. Clearly, Ro sees her charge likes Sophie, and more than once I wished she would win one of their bets and dare Keefe to tell Sophie he likes her. They bring out the best in each other and Keefe is always trying to cheer her up or make her smile and always tries to make amends for any actions he did that might have resulted in someone being hurt or manipulated. Keefe was one of the saving graces in this book. I love his snarky attitude and how he and Sophie have a better relationship that her and Fitz. With Fitz it seems more like she sees him like this savior type who "rescued" her and sent her to go live in paradise. With Keefe, it feels more real, like their shared troubles of having difficult childhoods and having to go through huge life-changing revelations gives them more of a connection than just Sophie's admiration of Fitz. <br />Fitz always came off as the knight-in-shining-armor who never had a problematic day in his life, and when stuff goes seriously wrong he handles it in the most hurtful and outrageous ways. I've always liked that each of the characters (except for the Vackers really) have had to struggle with lots of painful elements that really shed light on the fact that the elves do not live in a perfect world and that lives are altered for the worse when things are covered up rather than working on preventative measures. Tam and Linh have to deal with having powers that many consider burdensome rather than useful talents, their parents want nothing to do with them, and now with them being separated its a wonder how these two will ever catch a break. Even the side characters are all struggling with problems: Marella has her mother and now her new pyrotechnical abilities, Forkle is still struggling with the loss of his sibling, and Keefe with both of his parents being an issue(thank god for Ro cause no one else seems to be looking out for him).<br /><br />I can honestly say the ending wasn't so much of a cliffhanger as a "well what did you expect with all the talk of DNA and the importance of the gene pool?" How else are the elves suppose to know if Sophie is related to any of her matches (That would be a pretty cruel twist if she was related to any of her crushes, though being related to the Vackers would be a hilarious way to cross off that match)? And I'm sure Forkle is going to give Sophie a very difficult time with not telling her the true identity of her parents. (Though don't the elves have DNA records of everyone born in the cities? So unless her biological parents were unregistered, couldn't Sophie just go up the council and say "here's some spit, now who are my parents so I can finally make out with my boyfriend?")<br /><br />With Sophie now unable to register for the match-making process, I find I'm looking forward to seeing if she and Keefe might get a chance to have a relationship. I feel that with Fitz and his new responsibility to try and fix the Vacker name, he's going to be judged more harshly for his matches and be a lot more pressured with finding his "hopeful".<br /><br />I hope things do pick up from now on and that more will be revealed about both organizations so that we are not left having to question everything and still be left in the dark. Here's to book 8 being a potential hopeful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4237756995936296117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2551921743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2551921743" />
    <a title="gwen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83999913-gwen"><img alt="gwen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573788723p2/83999913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2551921743?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gwen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gwen" href="/user/show/83999913-gwen">gwen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481497435" href="/book/show/38364757-flashback">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=imaginative">imaginative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=elves">elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=superpowers">superpowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83999913-gwen?shelf=reconciliation">reconciliation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2551921743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8592644667099293002">This is not what I was expecting. And I don't mean that in a good way. I was looking for an epic, action-packed, thrilling conclusion with a (finally) resolved ending. <i>Flashback</i> wasn't particularly epic, or particularly exceptional. As ashamed as I to admit this, it was actually kind of… boring. <br/><b>It was too long.</b><br/>Don't get me wrong—I love big books. <i>Flashback</i> was a fat tome of training, crushing, training some more, being afraid of killing people, crushing some more, training some more, and oops, </span>
  <span id="freeText8592644667099293002" style="display:none">This is not what I was expecting. And I don't mean that in a good way. I was looking for an epic, action-packed, thrilling conclusion with a (finally) resolved ending. <i>Flashback</i> wasn't particularly epic, or particularly exceptional. As ashamed as I to admit this, it was actually kind of… boring. <br><b>It was too long.</b><br>Don't get me wrong—I love big books. <i>Flashback</i> was a fat tome of training, crushing, training some more, being afraid of killing people, crushing some more, training some more, and oops, oh no—the Neverseen won <i>again</i>. Sophie and her friends seem to have endless resolves to once and for all outsmart the Neverseen, but <i>every single time</i> they fail. Maybe the Neverseen are big and bad and powerful, but they honestly can't be that invincible. <br><b>Foster-Keefe died.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549193505ra/27008984.gif" width="265" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>LIKE LITERALLY WTF<br>I have always been an avid shipper of Foster-Keefe and <i>not</i> Sophitz. I literally want to get Grady to make Fitz jump off a cliff or something, he's that annoying. He's just there to be Sophie's crush and has zero personality. Keefe, on the other hand, is the epitome of amazing. Like honestly, Messenger, can't you at least make Sophie <i>fall in love with the right person??</i><br><b>The cliffhanger was… meh.</b><br>And although the twist at the end was certainly surprisingly, <b>it didn't make sense</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why would Sophie be unmatchable? She does have five billion abilities, but I don't think she's <i>unmatchable</i>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Someone needs to die.</b><br>Don't tell me that Mr. Forkle has died or Brant or Jolie or Kenric. Those people weren't main enough to cause a real impact. I think Fitz or Biana needs to die, or maybe Grady and Edaline (now <i>that</i> would be sad). <br><br><i>Flashback</i> left many things unresolved and I was frequently irritated by the romance. I thought this would a thrilling ending with no limit to the action. But no, the book just drags on and on, and although I did like it moderately (who <i>doesn't</i> love Keefe?) it wasn't the best in the series.<br><br><i>The first verse was a celebration of night—a ballad of dancing shadows and creeping mist and all the tony, soothing shifts that let the world slip into restful slumber. <br>But as the lyrics carried on, they curved to an ode of darkness itself. A reminder that there was purpose and power, even in the blackest place. Even to the shadows within herself. <br>The anger.<br>And doubts.<br>And sadness.<br>The memories that were too painful to replay.</i> - Page 833</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8592644667099293002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2974707484?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/4988733-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481497435" href="/book/show/38364757-flashback">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4988733-alexa?shelf=2020-flights-of-fantasy">2020-flights-of-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4988733-alexa?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2974707484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4002999785670579808">3.5 stars, but worth rounding up for the precious hilarious heartfelt wonderful bits that were sprinkled all throughout.<br/><br/>Prior to picking this one up, I’d seen that the general consensus about this book was that it was one of the least favored in the series. Truth is, I can see why, as it is probably my least favorite so far (and that doesn’t really amount to much considering I still enjoyed it).<br/><br/>Pros: Got some quality time with my favorite characters, learned more about the world, new characters </span>
  <span id="freeText4002999785670579808" style="display:none">3.5 stars, but worth rounding up for the precious hilarious heartfelt wonderful bits that were sprinkled all throughout.<br /><br />Prior to picking this one up, I’d seen that the general consensus about this book was that it was one of the least favored in the series. Truth is, I can see why, as it is probably my least favorite so far (and that doesn’t really amount to much considering I still enjoyed it).<br /><br />Pros: Got some quality time with my favorite characters, learned more about the world, new characters to like, A+ humor and banter and some really nice heartfelt moments<br /><br />Cons: A lack of on the page time for my favorites (who felt underutilized), recycled plot structure that didn’t quite pack the same punch, a heavy-handed touch on the ship (1/2 of whom I was particularly not happy with in this one)c a slightly underwhelming third act (including reveals)<br /><br />Just to reiterate, even with the cons, I did like this book. I still got swept up in the story (which was super compulsively readable as usual) and it was fun to discuss with Macky as I read! <br /><br />But that ending definitely makes me curious about how the next books is going to go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4002999785670579808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2297138168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2297138168" />
    <a title="Eva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65204187-eva"><img alt="Eva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541942357p2/65204187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2297138168?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eva" href="/user/show/65204187-eva">Eva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65204187-eva?shelf=keeper-of-the-lost-cities">keeper-of-the-lost-cities</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65204187-eva?shelf=elves">elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65204187-eva?shelf=special-powers">special-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65204187-eva?shelf=such-a-good-book">such-a-good-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65204187-eva?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65204187-eva?shelf=i-love-this-book">i-love-this-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2297138168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18106774203823138615">Note: Direct spoilers will be hidden, but the whole of the review will contain small details about pacing and my opinions on the writing. Certain aspects of the story will be alluded to.<br/><br/>I finally read it! I must say, it was not my favorite KotLC book. I believe there were 289 pages spent in the hospital wing, so it did drag in parts. Not that Mrs. Messenger is beginning to have a shortage of ideas, because this books brought plenty of new things to the table. But, it was written in such a way th</span>
  <span id="freeText18106774203823138615" style="display:none">Note: Direct spoilers will be hidden, but the whole of the review will contain small details about pacing and my opinions on the writing. Certain aspects of the story will be alluded to.<br /><br />I finally read it! I must say, it was not my favorite KotLC book. I believe there were 289 pages spent in the hospital wing, so it did drag in parts. Not that Mrs. Messenger is beginning to have a shortage of ideas, because this books brought plenty of new things to the table. But, it was written in such a way that all the action was packed into one part, and the rest just dragged along. I believe I would have enjoyed this book more had the action been spread out more throughout the entire book, and the hospital wing time has been written in a shorter length. Action needs to be evenly dispersed throughout the book; this book had a small burst of action, then a long time of recovery and preparation, and then the rest of the action packed into the last parts of the book.<br /><br />That being said, this book was not like I was afraid it might be: a repeat of Nightfall. Characters rise and fell, relationships were strengthened in some ways and lessened in others, and new characters were introduced. Aspects of the elvin world previously unseen were brought to light, and Shannon Messenger made some bold moves that many fans may dislike. One of my favorites of these moves (I actually predicted this before reading it) was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that Tam was forced into joining the Neverseen. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I mean, not everything can be perfect, can it? It was aspects like this that gave this book a different edge than Nightfall.<br /><br />When reading this book, you will only appreciate it as a true Keeper fan like myself. Power through the parts that drag, because the action will come! And enjoy the book for what it is: a small part of a larger story that is so much more than one book could hold. As part of the series, it is a necessary piece.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18106774203823138615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zaBDpl/gs02bu78TZaEJf4jCzmn9e+OFPlDkgD0A+oFJAOntyUOiNAX6AmqSPONuESw3H5DLp9xQ1MNzE6gmtg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2t/f45/zAqHPICL65tAl1GDgG5pJoMmaiaeWqJ9nCFVef3WoCVAT2FFhn4MRTc/F+Q7i7CQQjcPnI7Fbsc/UYg==')})
  }
//]]>
